<div id="review_1420417355" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1420417355" />
    <a title="Thomas Strömquist" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32669562-thomas-str-mquist"><img alt="Thomas Strömquist" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590007844p2/32669562.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1420417355?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas Strömquist" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas Strömquist" href="/user/show/32669562-thomas-str-mquist">Thomas Strömquist</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback " href="/book/show/27400173-summer-of-night">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32669562-thomas-str-mquist?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32669562-thomas-str-mquist?shelf=book-collection">book-collection</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1420417355" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7587150873518495778">First of 2016 - Buddy read with Edward Lorn - first one to enter my favorite shelf in quite some time!<br/><br/>In what should be a perfectly normal summer of 1960 in Elm Haven, a group of kids gets aware that a great evil is waking up. On the last day of school, one boy vanishes and other strange things starts happening. All seems to be connected to their school itself, the Old Central. As the kids starts to tentatively investigate some of the odd happenings, sightings and strange behaving townspeople th</span>
  <span id="freeText7587150873518495778" style="display:none">First of 2016 - Buddy read with Edward Lorn - first one to enter my favorite shelf in quite some time!<br /><br />In what should be a perfectly normal summer of 1960 in Elm Haven, a group of kids gets aware that a great evil is waking up. On the last day of school, one boy vanishes and other strange things starts happening. All seems to be connected to their school itself, the Old Central. As the kids starts to tentatively investigate some of the odd happenings, sightings and strange behaving townspeople they are targeted and soon realize that they have to pull together and fight what's threatening not only them, but time is running out.<br /><br />Superbly told and absolutely riveting coming-of-age-cum-horror story, quite certainly owing a lot to King's IT, but a great book in its own rights. Characterization is wonderful and I have trouble remembering another book where 12-year old protagonists worked so well (the little brother is a mere 8 and he works too!) But it doesn't end there, the bullies, the girls, the scary adults and the parents and uncles (and not least grandmother Memo!) are greatly drawn too and this really enhances the experience. And last, but not least, the Old Central itself (but here I got and advantage, since I went my first school years in a building that could easily have been a physical manifestation of this one - another experience enhancer I can tell you!) My favorite character is, however, the sister of the first boy taken, Cordie Cooke, a poor, gun-toting and strangely resourceful outsider girl who the boys have pinned as more or less certifiable. But, following a few close calls that comes to nothing thanks to her uncanny ability to be at the right place at the right (or perhaps that should be wrong) time, they come to depend on her quite a bit. Definitely no Beverly of IT, but certainly one you want on your team!<br /><br />Great build-up with top narrative and storytelling, then around the middle mark, the whole thing takes a tough and unexpected turn for the darker. Lastly, a model ending - suspenseful, but not unnecessarily drawn out. Basically, I thought everything in this book worked, I'm amazed that I haven't read it before and very happy that Edward wanted to read it with me. I will surely search out more by Simmons.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7587150873518495778" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText13235641433803007478" style="display:none">9/10<br /><br /><b>My 500th book since records began (i.e. Goodreads)</b><br /><br />I was totally unaware of this little beast until I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2605674103?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener"> Dan’s great review</a> that lured me in and it was everything he said and more. What a little treat for my earbuds! <br /><br />I’m drawn to these coming of age tales set in a time long before I was born in a land across the pond. Something about the innocence of youth in a time which, on the surface, seems simpler than life today. This is one of those stories but added in to it is a dormant horror element on a small rural town which suddenly decides to be no longer dormant. There is a large cast of characters fleshing out this local community and it did take a bit of time to remember who was who but it soon slotted in like a 1000 piece jigsaw. <br /><br />I did this in audiobook and it was by far the longest audiobook I’ve ever listened to coming in at over 22 hours and the narrator was decent enough but there was only one speed so when something tense was happening it was confusing at first as the pace was the same as if he was describing a sandwich. That aside this was great in audio mainly down to how good the story was. I went out of my way to listen to it which says a lot. My commute would become slightly longer or I would pray to the traffic gods. <br /><br />Don’t take my review as a measuring stick for this. Check out Dan’s review and give it a try. I’d not heard of it prior to that but I’m sure glad I made the effort to hunt it down once I had!</span>

<div id="review_2698263378" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2698263378" />
    <a title="Dean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18009940-dean"><img alt="Dean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605802027p2/18009940.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2698263378?book_show_action=true">Feb 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dean" href="/user/show/18009940-dean">Dean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312550677" href="/book/show/9897624-summer-of-night">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2698263378" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18087319210362511921">It's a rainy, grey, uncomfortable and cheerless Sunday morning in January..<br/>This will bring me in the right mood for writting a review about "Summer Of Night" by Dan Simmons.<br/>If you love horror novels, then you must be familiar with names like Stephen King or Dean Koontz..<br/>So, you can count Dan Simmons also to this club ..<br/><br/>I'm sitting here in my living room before my notebook, and asking myself how to review a novel like this!!!<br/>What about this:<br/>Awesome, gripping, tantalizing, or even a compulsive rea</span>
  <span id="freeText18087319210362511921" style="display:none">It's a rainy, grey, uncomfortable and cheerless Sunday morning in January..<br />This will bring me in the right mood for writting a review about "Summer Of Night" by Dan Simmons.<br />If you love horror novels, then you must be familiar with names like Stephen King or Dean Koontz..<br />So, you can count Dan Simmons also to this club ..<br /><br />I'm sitting here in my living room before my notebook, and asking myself how to review a novel like this!!!<br />What about this:<br />Awesome, gripping, tantalizing, or even a compulsive read..<br />Yeah, yeah,I know it's not bad.. but I rather stick with this: an encarnated literary nightmare reminiscence of Stephen Kings "IT" and sparkling with the uniqueness, daunting and paralizing imagination by such a master of his craft which indeed is Dan Simmons!!!<br /><br />Let me tell you, that if you haven't read this novel yet, then be assured that it awaits you an experience out of the ordinary and out of all expectations that you possible could bear or imagine!!!<br />No wonder that Stephen King said: "I am in awe of Dan Simmons"..<br /><br />Well, the reason I've had to give "Summer Of Night" four stars resides in the fact that this novel is written with so much originality and also fantasy, that it never becomes dull or boring, not even for a second..<br />The characters are also develop in such manner that the reader can easily identify with them, and connect powerfull with their world and what's happening all around them!!!<br /><br />"Summer Of Night" is also a fast paced horror thriller, and it has scared the bejessus out of me !!!<br />..And that often!!!!<br />I'm not ashamed and want to say it aloud: it seriously scared me in ways I didn't expect at all!!! <br /><br />Also it was unputdownable, I could not put it down and was forced like under a spell to read on and on..till far late in the night!!!<br />Despite being tired and having itching, red eyes..<br />Although the style used by Dan Simmons in taking his time and describing effusively and gushingly the surroundings, persons, the situations, and moods in the story, it never gave me the impression of reading a monster novel with nearly 500 pages!!!<br /><br />Out of the blue ..<br />and into the dark..<br /><br />Like in Stephen Kings novel "IT", a bunch of children must fight and confront the unspeakable evil in a small town!!<br />Only they can stop it!!!<br />But not Pennywise the clown this time!!!<br />A cursed bell plays an important part in the story..<br />Then you have here indeed unique horror personalities born out of a living nightmare..<br />This is a more serious horror, more deeply rootet in blood, doom,and disaster !!!<br /><br />Also this is a complex written work, with a lot of stuff happening all the time..<br />Worthy to be read again and again..<br /><br />If you love spooky, well written horror novels, then this is for you!!!<br />I for my part have enjoyed it very much..<br />And Dan Simmons is a writer I will keep following!!!<br /><br />Happy reading to all my goodread friends<br />Dean;)))</span>
  <a data-text-id="18087319210362511921" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1351720594" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1351720594" />
    <a title="Cindy Newton" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6082517-cindy-newton"><img alt="Cindy Newton" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1432075684p2/6082517.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1351720594?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cindy Newton" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cindy Newton" href="/user/show/6082517-cindy-newton">Cindy Newton</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/34535733-summer-of-night">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082517-cindy-newton?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082517-cindy-newton?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082517-cindy-newton?shelf=audible">audible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082517-cindy-newton?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1351720594" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9832698641118516623">I loved this! I listened to it on audiobook, and found myself making excuses to run errands so I could listen in the car. It's the tale of a group of young kids and the hellish summer they spend battling the forces of evil in the shape of horrendous monsters. It reminded me a lot of <i>It</i>, but at the same time, it is a completely different story.<br/><br/>The mayhem starts quickly as the story opens on the last day of school. As the last bell sounds and the student body rushes out to begin summer, there is o</span>
  <span id="freeText9832698641118516623" style="display:none">I loved this! I listened to it on audiobook, and found myself making excuses to run errands so I could listen in the car. It's the tale of a group of young kids and the hellish summer they spend battling the forces of evil in the shape of horrendous monsters. It reminded me a lot of <i>It</i>, but at the same time, it is a completely different story.<br /><br />The mayhem starts quickly as the story opens on the last day of school. As the last bell sounds and the student body rushes out to begin summer, there is one student who doesn't leave--and never will. From then on the book alternates between hair-raising scenes of horror and descriptions of children enjoying their summer break, reminding you that they are, after all, just kids. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[And one scene had me howling in anguish and disbelief--NO!! NOT DUANE!!! I couldn't BELIEVE they actually got him. It broke my heart! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I think it is interesting that you give me a book like this, about a ragtag group of 10- and 11-year olds fighting against unimaginable horrors with a grim intensity and I'm completely spellbound; give me a book about teenagers saving the world and my primary reaction is skepticism. Part of it is that I teach teenagers. I've seen their work; their inability to understand the simplest directions no matter how many times you repeat them, to master the complexity of such problems as putting their entire name at the top of their paper . . . these things do not inspire me with confidence in their ability to save all of mankind. ;) I think it is also because the kids' fight against evil is saturated with the magic of childhood. As we read, we are transported back to that time when magic was possible and anything could happen, when monsters DID dwell in dark closets and under the bed. In these stories, the impossible becomes possible and things we never dreamed of become real. In teen years, that magic fades and the only impossible things that become real are hormone-driven. In the world of children, the kids are battling these forces of evil without adult help. The adults, having lost their magic long ago, are completely blind to the forces of evil. They are unaware that a battle is going on at all. These kids are on their own. The teenagers, however, in many popular YA books, step in when the moronic adults have proven themselves completely unable to deal with the situation. They then run rings around the moronic adults and save the day. This is less believable to me than the story based on the magic of childhood. <br /><br />So if you're a fan of horror and childhood nostalgia, this book is for you! I highly recommend!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9832698641118516623" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fswZb5YcK1Qos6blSc7d5Rnpf3E3j4mIYMLq4eGe66194fUOJlfOzHBOfXKpxvI+LJW1szvC4y9zbZlQ0kChVQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ktq5F5F9nJEFWL5chmErxN4rR0IntjwToIXoaokf43yR91V2ITZ5CV2lZctmaQQf61eNgCv7VrSzKpvbusGphA==')})
  }

People either work for the paper mill up the Tecumseh River, or <\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText1880818897901552439\" style=\"display:none\">An Alabama boy’s innocence is shaken by murder and madness in the 1960s South in this novel by the New York Times–bestselling author of Swan Song.\n\nIt’s 1964 in idyllic Zephyr, Alabama. People either work for the paper mill up the Tecumseh River, or for the local dairy. It’s a simple life, but it stirs the impressionable imagination of twelve-year-old aspiring writer Cory Mackenson. He’s certain he’s sensed spirits whispering in the churchyard. He’s heard of the weird bootleggers who lurk in the dark outside of town. He’s seen a flood leave Main Street crawling with snakes. Cory thrills to all of it as only a young boy can.\n \nThen one morning, while accompanying his father on his milk route, he sees a car careen off the road and slowly sink into fathomless Saxon’s Lake. His father dives into the icy water to rescue the driver, and finds a beaten corpse, naked and handcuffed to the steering wheel—a copper wire tightened around the stranger’s neck. In time, the townsfolk seem to forget all about the unsolved murder. But Cory and his father can’t.\n \nTheir search for the truth is a journey into a world where innocence and evil collide. What lies before them is the stuff of fear and awe, magic and madness, fantasy and reality. As Cory wades into the deep end of Zephyr and all its mysteries, he’ll discover that while the pleasures of childish things fade away, growing up can be a strange and beautiful ride.\n \n“Strongly echoing the childhood-elegies of King and Bradbury, and every bit their equal,” Boy’s Life, a winner of both the Bram Stoker and World Fantasy Awards, represents a brilliant blend of mystery and rich atmosphere, the finest work of one of today’s most accomplished writers (Kirkus Reviews).<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"1880818897901552439\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2687.Dan_Simmons">About Dan Simmons</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/2687.Dan_Simmons"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1427999015p3/2687.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/2687.Dan_Simmons">Dan Simmons
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
9,053
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7639357192644752921"><b>Dan Simmons</b> grew up in various cities and small towns in the Midwest, including Brimfield, Illinois, which was the source of his fictional "Elm Haven" in 1991's SUMMER OF NIGHT and 2002's A WINTER HAUNTING. Dan received a B.A. in English from Wabash College in 1970, winning a national Phi Beta Kappa Award during his senior year for excellence in fiction, journalism and art. <br/><br/>Dan received his Master</span>
  <span id="freeText7639357192644752921" style="display:none"><b>Dan Simmons</b> grew up in various cities and small towns in the Midwest, including Brimfield, Illinois, which was the source of his fictional "Elm Haven" in 1991's SUMMER OF NIGHT and 2002's A WINTER HAUNTING. Dan received a B.A. in English from Wabash College in 1970, winning a national Phi Beta Kappa Award during his senior year for excellence in fiction, journalism and art. <br /><br />Dan received his Masters in Education from Washington University in St. Louis in 1971. He then worked in elementary education for 18 years—2 years in Missouri, 2 years in Buffalo, New York—one year as a specially trained BOCES "resource teacher" and another as a sixth-grade teacher—and 14 years in Colorado.<br /> <br /> ABOUT DAN<br /> Biographic Sketch <br /> <br />His last four years in teaching were spent creating, coordinating, and teaching in APEX, an extensive gifted/talented program serving 19 elementary schools and some 15,000 potential students. During his years of teaching, he won awards from the Colorado Education Association and was a finalist for the Colorado Teacher of the Year. He also worked as a national language-arts consultant, sharing his own "Writing Well" curriculum which he had created for his own classroom. Eleven and twelve-year-old students in Simmons' regular 6th-grade class averaged junior-year in high school writing ability according to annual standardized and holistic writing assessments. Whenever someone says "writing can't be taught," Dan begs to differ and has the track record to prove it. Since becoming a full-time writer, Dan likes to visit college writing classes, has taught in New Hampshire's Odyssey writing program for adults, and is considering hosting his own Windwalker Writers' Workshop.<br /><br />Dan's first published story appeared on Feb. 15, 1982, the day his daughter, Jane Kathryn, was born. He's always attributed that coincidence to "helping in keeping things in perspective when it comes to the relative importance of writing and life."<br /><br />Dan has been a full-time writer since 1987 and lives along the Front Range of Colorado—in the same town where he taught for 14 years—with his wife, Karen, his daughter, Jane, (when she's home from Hamilton College) and their Pembroke Welsh Corgi, Fergie. He does much of his writing at Windwalker—their mountain property and cabin at 8,400 feet of altitude at the base of the Continental Divide, just south of Rocky Mountain National Park. An 8-ft.-tall sculpture of the Shrike—a thorned and frightening character from the four Hyperion/Endymion novels—was sculpted by an ex-student and friend, Clee Richeson, and the sculpture now stands guard near the isolated cabin.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7639357192644752921" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
